         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Salar_de_Uyuni" title="Salar de Uyuni">
          Salar de Uyuni
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cordillera_Central_Bolivia.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1038" data-file-width="2759" height="83" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Cordillera_Central_Bolivia.jpg/220px-Cordillera_Central_Bolivia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Cordillera_Central_Bolivia.jpg/330px-Cordillera_Central_Bolivia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Cordillera_Central_Bolivia.jpg/440px-Cordillera_Central_Bolivia.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cordillera_Central_Bolivia.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Bolivia)" title="Cordillera Central (Bolivia)">
          Cordillera Central
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sajama_National_Park.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2224" data-file-width="3055" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Sajama_National_Park.jpg/220px-Sajama_National_Park.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Sajama_National_Park.jpg/330px-Sajama_National_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Sajama_National_Park.jpg/440px-Sajama_National_Park.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sajama_National_Park.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Nevado_Sajama" title="Nevado Sajama">
          Nevado Sajama
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Bolivia is located in the central zone of
       <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">
        South America
       </a>
       , between 57°26'–69°38'W and 9°38'–22°53'S. With an area of 1,098,581 square kilometres (424,164 sq mi), Bolivia is the world's 28th-largest country, and the fifth largest country in South America,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       extending from the
       <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">
        Central Andes
       </a>
       through part of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">
         Gran Chaco
        </a>
       </i>
       as far as the
       <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">
        Amazon
       </a>
       . The geographic center of the country is the so-called
       <i>
        Puerto Estrella
       </i>
       ("Star Port") on the
       <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_(Bolivia)" title="Río Grande (Bolivia)">
        Río Grande
       </a>
       , in
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%91uflo_de_Ch%C3%A1vez_Province" title="Ñuflo de Chávez Province">
        Ñuflo de Chávez Province
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Department,_Bolivia" title="Santa Cruz Department, Bolivia">
        Santa Cruz Department
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The geography of the country exhibits a great variety of terrain and climates. Bolivia has a high level of
       <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">
        biodiversity
       </a>
       , considered one of the greatest in the world, as well as several
       <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">
        ecoregions
       </a>
       with ecological sub-units such as the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Altiplano" title="Altiplano">
         Altiplano
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest" title="Tropical rainforest">
        tropical rainforests
       </a>
       (including
       <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">
        Amazon rainforest
       </a>
       ), dry
       <a href="/wiki/Valley" title="Valley">
        valleys
       </a>
       , and the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Chiquitania" title="Chiquitania">
         Chiquitania
        </a>
       </i>
       , which is a
       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_grasslands,_savannas,_and_shrublands" title="Tropical and subtropical grasslands, savannas, and shrublands">
        tropical savanna
       </a>
       . These areas feature enormous variations in altitude, from an elevation of 6,542 metres (21,463 ft) above sea level in
       <a href="/wiki/Nevado_Sajama" title="Nevado Sajama">
        Nevado Sajama
       </a>
       to nearly 70 metres (230 ft) along the
       <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_River" title="Paraguay River">
        Paraguay River
       </a>
       . Although a country of great geographic diversity, Bolivia has remained a
       <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">
        landlocked country
       </a>
       since the
       <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">
        War of the Pacific
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Bolivia can be divided into three
       <a href="/wiki/Physical_geography" title="Physical geography">
        physiographic
       </a>
       regions:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <b>
         The Andean region
        </b>
        in the southwest spans 28% of the national territory, extending over 307,603 square kilometres (118,766 sq mi). This area is located above 3,000 metres (9,800 ft) altitude and is located between two big Andean chains, the
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cordillera_Occidental_(Bolivia)" title="Cordillera Occidental (Bolivia)">
          Cordillera Occidental
         </a>
        </i>
        ("Western Range") and the
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Bolivia)" title="Cordillera Central (Bolivia)">
          Cordillera Central
         </a>
        </i>
        ("Central Range"), with some of the highest spots in the
        <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">
         Americas
        </a>
        such as the
        <a href="/wiki/Nevado_Sajama" title="Nevado Sajama">
         Nevado Sajama
        </a>
        , with an altitude of 6,542 metres (21,463 ft), and the
        <a href="/wiki/Illimani" title="Illimani">
         Illimani
        </a>
        , at 6,462 metres (21,201 ft). Also located in the Cordillera Central is
        <a href="/wiki/Lake_Titicaca" title="Lake Titicaca">
         Lake Titicaca
        </a>
        , the highest commercially navigable lake in the world and the largest lake in South America;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
         <a href="#cite_note-45">
          [45]
         </a>
        </sup>
        the lake is shared with
        <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">
         Peru
        </a>
        . Also in this region are the
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Altiplano" title="Altiplano">
          Altiplano
         </a>
        </i>
        and the
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Salar_de_Uyuni" title="Salar de Uyuni">
          Salar de Uyuni
         </a>
        </i>
        , which is the largest
        <a href="/wiki/Salt_pan_(geology)" title="Salt pan (geology)">
         salt flat
        </a>
        in the world and an important source of
        <a href="/wiki/Lithium" title="Lithium">
         lithium
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <b>
         Sub-Andean region
        </b>
        in the center and south of the country is an intermediate region between the
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Altiplano" title="Altiplano">
          Altiplano
         </a>
        </i>
        and the eastern
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Plain" title="Plain">
          llanos
         </a>
        </i>
        (plain); this region comprises 13% of the territory of Bolivia, extending over 142,815 km
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        (55,141 sq mi), and encompassing the Bolivian valleys and the Yungas region. It is distinguished by its farming activities and its temperate climate.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <b>
         Llanos region
        </b>
        in the northeast comprises 59% of the territory, with 648,163 km
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        (250,257 sq mi). It is located to the north of the
        <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Bolivia)" title="Cordillera Central (Bolivia)">
         Cordillera Central
        </a>
        and extends from the Andean foothills to the
        <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_River" title="Paraguay River">
         Paraguay River
        </a>
        . It is a region of flat land and small plateaus, all covered by extensive rain forests containing enormous biodiversity. The region is below 400 metres (1,300 ft) above sea level.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Bolivia has three
       <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">
        drainage basins
       </a>
       :
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The first is the
        <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">
         Amazon Basin
        </a>
        , also called the North Basin (724,000 km
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        (280,000 sq mi)/66% of the territory). The rivers of this basin generally have big
        <a href="/wiki/Meander" title="Meander">
         meanders
        </a>
        which form lakes such as
        <a href="/wiki/Murillo_Lake" title="Murillo Lake">
         Murillo Lake
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Pando_Department" title="Pando Department">
         Pando Department
        </a>
        . The main Bolivian
        <a href="/wiki/Tributary" title="Tributary">
         tributary
        </a>
        to the Amazon basin is the
        <a href="/wiki/Mamor%C3%A9_River" title="Mamoré River">
         Mamoré River
        </a>
        , with a length of 2,000 km (1,200 mi) running north to the confluence with the
        <a href="/wiki/Beni_River" title="Beni River">
         Beni River
        </a>
        , 1,113 km (692 mi) in length and the second most important river of the country. The Beni River, along with the
        <a href="/wiki/Madeira_River" title="Madeira River">
         Madeira River
        </a>
        , forms the main tributary of the
        <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">
         Amazon River
        </a>
        . From east to west, the basin is formed by other important rivers, such as the
        <a href="/wiki/Madre_de_Dios_River" title="Madre de Dios River">
         Madre de Dios River
        </a>
        , the
        <a href="/wiki/Orthon_River" title="Orthon River">
         Orthon River
        </a>
        , the
        <a href="/wiki/Abuna_River" title="Abuna River">
         Abuna River
        </a>
        , the
        <a href="/wiki/Yata_River" title="Yata River">
         Yata River
        </a>
        , and the
        <a href="/wiki/Guapor%C3%A9_River" title="Guaporé River">
         Guaporé River
        </a>
        . The most important lakes are
        <a href="/wiki/Rogaguado_Lake" title="Rogaguado Lake">
         Rogaguado Lake
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Rogagua_Lake" title="Rogagua Lake">
         Rogagua Lake
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Jara_Lake" title="Jara Lake">
         Jara Lake
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        The second is the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rio_de_la_Plata_Basin" title="Rio de la Plata Basin">
         Rio de la Plata Basin
        </a>
        , also called the South Basin (229,500 km
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        (88,600 sq mi)/21% of the territory). The tributaries in this basin are in general less abundant than the ones forming the Amazon Basin. The Rio de la Plata Basin is mainly formed by the
        <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_River" title="Paraguay River">
         Paraguay River
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Pilcomayo_River" title="Pilcomayo River">
         Pilcomayo River
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Bermejo_River" title="Bermejo River">
         Bermejo River
        </a>
        . The most important lakes are
        <a href="/wiki/Uberaba_Lake" title="Uberaba Lake">
         Uberaba Lake
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Mandior%C3%A9_Lake" title="Mandioré Lake">
         Mandioré Lake
        </a>
        , both located in the Bolivian marshland.
       </li>
       <li>
        The third basin is the
        <b>
         Central Basin
        </b>
        , which is an
        <a href="/wiki/Endorheic_basin" title="Endorheic basin">
         endorheic basin
        </a>
        (145,081 square kilometres (56,016 sq mi)/13% of the territory). The
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Altiplano" title="Altiplano">
          Altiplano
         </a>
        </i>
        has large numbers of lakes and rivers that do not run into any ocean because they are enclosed by the Andean mountains. The most important river is the
        <a href="/wiki/Desaguadero_River_(Bolivia)" title="Desaguadero River (Bolivia)">
         Desaguadero River
        </a>
        , with a length of 436 km (271 mi), the longest river of the
        <i>
         Altiplano
        </i>
        ; it begins in
        <a href="/wiki/Lake_Titicaca" title="Lake Titicaca">
         Lake Titicaca
        </a>
        and then runs in a southeast direction to
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poop%C3%B3_Lake" title="Poopó Lake">
         Poopó Lake
        </a>
        . The basin is then formed by Lake Titicaca, Lake Poopó, the Desaguadero River, and great salt flats, including the
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Salar_de_Uyuni" title="Salar de Uyuni">
          Salar de Uyuni
         </a>
        </i>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Coipasa_Lake" title="Coipasa Lake">
         Coipasa Lake
        </a>
        .
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sustaining_water_supplies">
        Sustaining water supplies
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Sustaining water supplies">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Deforestation in upper river basins has caused environmental problems, including soil erosion and declining water quality. An innovative project to try and remedy this situation involves landholders in upstream areas being paid by downstream water users to conserve forests. The landholders receive $20 to conserve the trees, avoid polluting livestock practices, and enhance the biodiversity and forest carbon on their land. They receive $30, which purchases a beehive, to compensate for conservation for two hectares of water-sustaining forest for five years. Honey revenue per hectare of forest is $5 per year, so within five years, the landholder has sold $50 of honey.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The project is being conducted by
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fundaci%C3%B3n_Natura_Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fundación Natura Bolivia (page does not exist)">
        Fundación Natura Bolivia
       </a>
       and Rare Conservation, with support from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_%26_Development_Knowledge_Network" title="Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network">
        Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">
        Geology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Bolivia" title="Geology of Bolivia">
        geology of Bolivia
       </a>
       comprises a variety of different
       <a href="/wiki/Lithology" title="Lithology">
        lithologies
       </a>
       as well as
       <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">
        tectonic
       </a>
       and sedimentary environments. On a synoptic scale, geological units coincide with topographical units. Most elementally, the country is divided into a mountainous western area affected by the
       <a href="/wiki/Subduction" title="Subduction">
        subduction
       </a>
       processes in the Pacific and an eastern lowlands of stable
       <a href="/wiki/Platform_(geology)" title="Platform (geology)">
        platforms
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Shield_(geology)" title="Shield (geology)">
        shields
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bolivia_prec.tif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="662" data-file-width="878" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Bolivia_prec.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Bolivia_prec.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Bolivia_prec.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Bolivia_prec.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Bolivia_prec.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Bolivia_prec.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bolivia_prec.tif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Mean annual precipitation in Bolivia
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
          <a href="#cite_note-47">
           [47]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>

         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">

        </a>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Los_Yungas_La_Paz_-_Bolivia.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Los_Yungas_La_Paz_-_Bolivia.jpg/220px-Los_Yungas_La_Paz_-_Bolivia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Los_Yungas_La_Paz_-_Bolivia.jpg/330px-Los_Yungas_La_Paz_-_Bolivia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Los_Yungas_La_Paz_-_Bolivia.jpg/440px-Los_Yungas_La_Paz_-_Bolivia.jpg 2x" width="220"/>

        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Los_Yungas_La_Paz_-_Bolivia.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Los Yungas,
         <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">
          La Paz
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The climate of Bolivia varies drastically from one eco-region to the other, from the tropics in the eastern
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Plain" title="Plain">
         llanos
        </a>
       </i>
       to a
       <a href="/wiki/Polar_climate" title="Polar climate">
        polar climate
       </a>
       in the western Andes. The summers are warm, humid in the east and dry in the west, with rains that often modify temperatures, humidity, winds,
       <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure" title="Atmospheric pressure">
        atmospheric pressure
       </a>
       and evaporation, yielding very different climates in different areas. When the climatological phenomenon known as
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o-Southern_Oscillation" title="El Niño-Southern Oscillation">
         El Niño
        </a>
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       takes place, it causes great alterations in the weather. Winters are very cold in the west, and it snows in the mountain ranges, while in the western regions, windy days are more common. The autumn is dry in the non-tropical regions.
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <i>
         Llanos
        </i>
        . A
        <a href="/wiki/Humidity" title="Humidity">
         humid
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">
         tropical climate
        </a>
        with an average temperature of 30 °C (86 °F). The wind coming from the
        <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">
         Amazon rainforest
        </a>
        causes significant rainfall. In May, there is low precipitation because of dry winds, and most days have clear skies. Even so, winds from the south, called
        <i>
         surazos
        </i>
        , can bring cooler temperatures lasting several days.
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Altiplano" title="Altiplano">
          Altiplano
         </a>
        </i>
        .
        <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">
         Desert
        </a>
        -
        <a href="/wiki/Polar_climate" title="Polar climate">
         Polar
        </a>
        climates, with strong and cold winds. The average temperature ranges from 15 to 20 °C. At night, temperatures descend drastically to slightly above 0 °C, while during the day, the weather is dry and
        <a href="/wiki/Sunlight" title="Sunlight">
         solar radiation
        </a>
        is high.
        <a href="/wiki/Ground_frost" title="Ground frost">
         Ground frosts
        </a>
        occur every month, and snow is frequent.
       </li>
       <li>
        Valleys and
        <i>
         Yungas
        </i>
        .
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperateness" title="Temperateness">
         Temperate
        </a>
        climate. The humid northeastern winds are pushed to the mountains, making this region very humid and rainy. Temperatures are cooler at higher elevations. Snow occurs at altitudes of 2,000 metres (6,600 ft).
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">
          Chaco
         </a>
        </i>
        .
        <a href="/wiki/Subtropics" title="Subtropics">
         Subtropical
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">
         semi-arid climate
        </a>
        . Rainy and humid in January and the rest of the year, with warm days and cool nights.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">
        Biodiversity
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madidi_Nationalpark_Amazonas_Bolivien.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="797" data-file-width="1200" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Madidi_Nationalpark_Amazonas_Bolivien.jpg/220px-Madidi_Nationalpark_Amazonas_Bolivien.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Madidi_Nationalpark_Amazonas_Bolivien.jpg/330px-Madidi_Nationalpark_Amazonas_Bolivien.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Madidi_Nationalpark_Amazonas_Bolivien.jpg/440px-Madidi_Nationalpark_Amazonas_Bolivien.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madidi_Nationalpark_Amazonas_Bolivien.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon_Basin" title="Amazon Basin">
          Amazon river basin
         </a>
         in Bolivia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Bolivia, with an enormous variety of
       <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">
        organisms
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">
        ecosystems
       </a>
       , is part of the "
       <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries#Cancún_initiative_and_declaration_of_like-minded_megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">
        Like-Minded Megadiverse Countries
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Bolivia's variable altitudes, ranging from 90–6,542 metres (295–21,463 ft) above sea level, allow for a vast biologic diversity. The territory of Bolivia comprises four types of
       <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">
        biomes
       </a>
       , 32 ecological regions, and 199 ecosystems. Within this geographic area there are several natural parks and reserves such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Noel_Kempff_Mercado_National_Park" title="Noel Kempff Mercado National Park">
        Noel Kempff Mercado National Park
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Madidi_National_Park" title="Madidi National Park">
        Madidi National Park
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Tunari_National_Park" title="Tunari National Park">
        Tunari National Park
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Avaroa_Andean_Fauna_National_Reserve" title="Eduardo Avaroa Andean Fauna National Reserve">
        Eduardo Avaroa Andean Fauna National Reserve
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Kaa-Iya_del_Gran_Chaco_National_Park_and_Integrated_Management_Natural_Area" title="Kaa-Iya del Gran Chaco National Park and Integrated Management Natural Area">
        Kaa-Iya del Gran Chaco National Park and Integrated Management Natural Area
       </a>
       , among others.
      </p>
      <p>
       Bolivia boasts over 17,000 species of seed plants, including over 1,200 species of
       <a href="/wiki/Fern" title="Fern">
        fern
       </a>
       , 1,500 species of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Marchantiophyta" title="Marchantiophyta">
         marchantiophyta
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Moss" title="Moss">
        moss
       </a>
       , and at least 800 species of
       <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">
        fungus
       </a>
       . In addition, there are more than 3,000 species of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medicinal_plant" title="Medicinal plant">
        medicinal plants
       </a>
       . Bolivia is considered the place of origin for such species as
       <a href="/wiki/Capsicum_pubescens" title="Capsicum pubescens">
        peppers
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Capsicum" title="Capsicum">
        chili peppers
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">
        peanuts
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Phaseolus_vulgaris" title="Phaseolus vulgaris">
        common beans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">
        yucca
       </a>
       , and several species of palm. Bolivia also naturally produces over 4,000 kinds of
       <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">
        potatoes
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Bolivia has more than 2,900 animal species, including 398 mammals, over 1,400 birds (about 14% of birds known in the world, being the sixth most diverse country in terms of bird species)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">
          <span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (February 2014)">
           unreliable source?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       , 204
       <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">
        amphibians
       </a>
       , 277
       <a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">
        reptiles
       </a>
       , and 635 fish, all
       <a href="/wiki/Fresh_water" title="Fresh water">
        fresh water
       </a>
       fish as Bolivia is a
       <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">
        landlocked country
       </a>
       . In addition, there are more than 3,000 types of
       <a href="/wiki/Lepidoptera" title="Lepidoptera">
        butterfly
       </a>
       , and more than 60
       <a href="/wiki/Domestication" title="Domestication">
        domestic animals
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Bolivia has gained global attention for its '
       <a href="/wiki/Law_of_the_Rights_of_Mother_Earth" title="Law of the Rights of Mother Earth">
        Law of the Rights of Mother Earth
       </a>
       ', which accords nature the same rights as humans.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Samaipata,_Bolivia.jpg" title="A view from the mountain in El Sauce overlooking Samaipata, Bolivia">
        <img alt="A view from the mountain in El Sauce overlooking Samaipata, Bolivia" data-file-height="1856" data-file-width="8192" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Samaipata%2C_Bolivia.jpg/1020px-Samaipata%2C_Bolivia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Samaipata%2C_Bolivia.jpg/1530px-Samaipata%2C_Bolivia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Samaipata%2C_Bolivia.jpg/2040px-Samaipata%2C_Bolivia.jpg 2x" width="1020"/>
       </a>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">
        Politics and government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Politics and government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Bolivia" title="Politics of Bolivia">
        Politics of Bolivia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Bolivia" title="Foreign relations of Bolivia">
        Foreign relations of Bolivia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LaPaz_Plaza_Pedro_Di_Murillo_10.2004.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="278" data-file-width="386" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/LaPaz_Plaza_Pedro_Di_Murillo_10.2004.jpg/220px-LaPaz_Plaza_Pedro_Di_Murillo_10.2004.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/LaPaz_Plaza_Pedro_Di_Murillo_10.2004.jpg/330px-LaPaz_Plaza_Pedro_Di_Murillo_10.2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4c/LaPaz_Plaza_Pedro_Di_Murillo_10.2004.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LaPaz_Plaza_Pedro_Di_Murillo_10.2004.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The government building of the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Bolivia" title="National Congress of Bolivia">
          National Congress of Bolivia
         </a>
         at the Plaza Murillo in central
         <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">
          La Paz
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Bolivia has been governed by democratically elected governments since 1982; prior to that, it was governed by various dictatorships. Presidents
       <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Siles_Zuazo" title="Hernán Siles Zuazo">
        Hernán Siles Zuazo
       </a>
       (1982–85) and
       <a href="/wiki/V%C3%ADctor_Paz_Estenssoro" title="Víctor Paz Estenssoro">
        Víctor Paz Estenssoro
       </a>
       (1985–89) began a tradition of ceding power peacefully which has continued, although two presidents have stepped down in the face of popular protests:
       <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_S%C3%A1nchez_de_Lozada" title="Gonzalo Sánchez de Lozada">
        Gonzalo Sánchez de Lozada
       </a>
       in 2003 and
       <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Mesa" title="Carlos Mesa">
        Carlos Mesa
       </a>
       in 2005.
      </p>
      <p>
       Bolivia's multiparty democracy has seen a wide variety of parties in the presidency and parliament, although the
       <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Nationalist_Movement" title="Revolutionary Nationalist Movement">
        Revolutionary Nationalist Movement
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Democratic_Action" title="Nationalist Democratic Action">
        Nationalist Democratic Action
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Left_Movement_(Bolivia)" title="Revolutionary Left Movement (Bolivia)">
        Revolutionary Left Movement
       </a>
       predominated from 1985 to 2005. The current president is
       <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">
        Evo Morales
       </a>
       , the first indigenous Bolivian to serve as head of state. Morales'
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Movement_for_Socialism_%E2%80%93_Political_Instrument_for_the_Sovereignty_of_the_Peoples" title="Movement for Socialism – Political Instrument for the Sovereignty of the Peoples">
        Movement for Socialism – Political Instrument for the Sovereignty of the Peoples
       </a>
       party was the first to win an outright presidential majority in four decades, doing so both in 2005 and 2009.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bolivia" title="Constitution of Bolivia">
        constitution
       </a>
       , drafted in 2006–07 and approved in 2009, provides for balanced executive, legislative, judicial, and electoral powers, as well as several levels of autonomy. The traditionally strong executive branch tends to overshadow the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Bolivia" title="National Congress of Bolivia">
        Congress
       </a>
       , whose role is generally limited to debating and approving legislation initiated by the executive. The judiciary, consisting of the
       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Bolivia" title="Supreme Court of Bolivia">
        Supreme Court
       </a>
       and departmental and lower courts, has long been riddled with corruption and inefficiency. Through revisions to the constitution in 1994, and subsequent laws, the government has initiated potentially far-reaching reforms in the judicial system as well as increasing decentralizing powers to departments, municipalities, and indigenous territories.
      </p>
      <p>
       The executive branch is headed by a President and Vice President, and consists of a variable number (currently, 20) of government
       <a href="/wiki/Ministry_(government_department)" title="Ministry (government department)">
        ministries
       </a>
       . The president is elected to a five-year term by
       <a href="/wiki/Direct_election" title="Direct election">
        popular vote
       </a>
       , and governs from the Presidential Palace (popularly called the Burnt Palace,
       <i>
        Palacio Quemado
       </i>
       ) in La Paz. In the case that no candidate receives an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Absolute_majority" title="Absolute majority">
        absolute majority
       </a>
       of the popular vote or more than 40% of the vote with an advantage of more than 10% over the second-place finisher, a run-off is to be held among the two candidates most voted.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presidencia.gob.bo_53-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-presidencia.gob.bo-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        Asamblea Legislativa Plurinacional
       </i>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Plurinational_Legislative_Assembly" title="Plurinational Legislative Assembly">
        Plurinational Legislative Assembly
       </a>
       or National Congress) has
       <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">
        two chambers
       </a>
       . The
       <i>
        Cámara de Diputados
       </i>
       (Chamber of Deputies) has 130 members elected to five-year terms, seventy from single-member districts (
       <i>
        circunscripciones
       </i>
       ), sixty by proportional representation, and seven by the minority indigenous peoples of seven departments. The
       <i>
        Cámara de Senadores
       </i>
       (Chamber of Senators) has 36 members (four per department). Members of the Assembly are elected to five-year terms. The body has its headquarters on the Plaza Murillo in La Paz, but also holds honorary sessions elsewhere in Bolivia. The Vice President serves as titular head of the combined Assembly.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Supremecourtbolivia.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Supremecourtbolivia.jpg/220px-Supremecourtbolivia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Supremecourtbolivia.jpg/330px-Supremecourtbolivia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Supremecourtbolivia.jpg/440px-Supremecourtbolivia.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Supremecourtbolivia.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Supreme Court Building in the capital of Bolivia,
         <a href="/wiki/Sucre" title="Sucre">
          Sucre
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The judiciary consists of the
       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Bolivia" title="Supreme Court of Bolivia">
        Supreme Court
       </a>
       , the Constitutional Tribunal, the Judiciary Council, Agrarian and Environmental Tribunal, and District (departmental) and lower courts. In October 2011, Bolivia held its first judicial elections to choose members of the national courts by popular vote, a reform brought about by Evo Morales.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Plurinational_Electoral_Organ" title="Plurinational Electoral Organ">
        Plurinational Electoral Organ
       </a>
       is an independent branch of government which replaced the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Electoral_Court_of_Bolivia" title="National Electoral Court of Bolivia">
        National Electoral Court
       </a>
       in 2010. The branch consists of the Supreme Electoral Tribunal, the nine Departmental Electoral Tribunals, Electoral Judges, the anonymously selected Juries at Election Tables, and Electoral Notaries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Wilfredo Ovando presides over the seven-member Supreme Electoral Tribunal. Its operations are mandated by the Constitution and regulated by the Electoral Regime Law (Law 026, passed 2010). The Organ's first elections were the country's first
       <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_judicial_election,_2011" title="Bolivian judicial election, 2011">
        judicial election
       </a>
       in October 2011, and five municipal special elections held in 2011.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Capital">
        Capital
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Capital">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Bolivia has its constitutionally recognized capital in Sucre, while La Paz is the seat of government. La Plata (now Sucre) was proclaimed provisional capital of the newly independent Alto Perú (later, Bolivia) on 1 July 1826.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DicGeo_55-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-DicGeo-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 12 July 1839, President
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Miguel_de_Velasco" title="José Miguel de Velasco">
        José Miguel de Velasco
       </a>
       proclaimed a law naming the city as the capital of Bolivia, and renaming it in honor of the revolutionary leader
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Sucre" title="Antonio José de Sucre">
        Antonio José de Sucre
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DicGeo_55-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-DicGeo-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Bolivian seat of government moved to
       <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">
        La Paz
       </a>
       at the start of the twentieth century, as a consequence of Sucre's relative remoteness from economic activity after the decline of
       <a href="/wiki/Potos%C3%AD" title="Potosí">
        Potosí
       </a>
       and its silver industry and of the Liberal Party in the War of 1899.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bolivia" title="Constitution of Bolivia">
        2009 Constitution
       </a>
       assigns the role of national capital to Sucre, not referring to La Paz in the text.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presidencia.gob.bo_53-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-presidencia.gob.bo-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition to being the constitutional capital, the Supreme Court of Bolivia is located in Sucre, making it the judicial capital. Nonetheless, the
       <a href="/wiki/Palacio_Quemado" title="Palacio Quemado">
        Palacio Quemado
       </a>
       (the Presidential Palace and seat of Bolivian
       <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">
        executive power
       </a>
       ) is located in La Paz, as are the National Congress and Plurinational Electoral Organ. La Paz thus continues to be the seat of government.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_crime">
        Law and crime
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Law and crime">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       There are 53
       <a href="/wiki/Prisons_in_Bolivia" title="Prisons in Bolivia">
        prisons in Bolivia
       </a>
       , which incarcerate around 8,700 people as of 2010
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       . The prisons are managed by the Penitentiary Regime Directorate (Spanish:
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         Dirección de Régimen Penintenciario
        </span>
       </i>
       ). There are 17 prisons in
       <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Bolivia" title="Departments of Bolivia">
        departmental
       </a>
       capital cities and 36 provincial prisons.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">
        Foreign relations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Despite losing its maritime coast, the so-called
       <a href="/wiki/Litoral_Department" title="Litoral Department">
        Litoral Department
       </a>
       , after the
       <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">
        War of the Pacific
       </a>
       , Bolivia has historically maintained, as a state policy, a maritime claim to that part of
       <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">
        Chile
       </a>
       ; the claim asks for sovereign access to the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       and its maritime space. The issue has also been presented before the
       <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">
        Organization of American States
       </a>
       ; in 1979, the OAS passed the
       <i>
        426 Resolution
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which declared that the Bolivian problem is a hemispheric problem. On 4 April 1884, a truce was signed with Chile, whereby Chile gave facilities of access to Bolivian products through
       <a href="/wiki/Antofagasta" title="Antofagasta">
        Antofagasta
       </a>
       , and freed the payment of export rights in the port of
       <a href="/wiki/Arica" title="Arica">
        Arica
       </a>
       . In October 1904, the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Peace_and_Friendship_(1904)" title="Treaty of Peace and Friendship (1904)">
        Treaty of Peace and Friendship
       </a>
       was signed, and Chile agreed to build a
       <a href="/wiki/Arica%E2%80%93La_Paz_railway" title="Arica–La Paz railway">
        railway between Arica and La Paz
       </a>
       , to improve access of Bolivian products to the ports.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        Special Economical Zone for Bolivia in Ilo
       </i>
       (ZEEBI) is a special economic area of 5 kilometres (3.1 miles) of maritime coast, and a total extension of 358
       <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">
        hectares
       </a>
       (880 acres), called Mar Bolivia ("Sea Bolivia"), where Bolivia may maintain a free port near
       <a href="/wiki/Ilo" title="Ilo">
        Ilo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">
        Peru
       </a>
       under its administration and operation
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">
          <span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (July 2013)">
           unreliable source?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       for a period of 99 years starting in 1992; once that time has passed, all the construction and territory revert to the Peruvian government. Since 1964, Bolivia has had its own port facilities in the
       <i>
        Bolivian Free Port
       </i>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario,_Santa_Fe" title="Rosario, Santa Fe">
        Rosario, Argentina
       </a>
       . This port is located on the
       <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_River" title="Paraná River">
        Paraná River
       </a>
       , which is directly connected to the Atlantic Ocean.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Military">
        Military
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Military">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Bolivia" title="Military of Bolivia">
        Bolivian military
       </a>
       comprises three branches:
       <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_Army" title="Bolivian Army">
        Ejército (Army)
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolivian_Naval_Force" title="Bolivian Naval Force">
        Naval (Navy)
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_Air_Force" title="Bolivian Air Force">
        Fuerza Aérea (Air Force)
       </a>
       . The legal age for voluntary admissions is 18; however, when the numbers are small the government recruits anyone as young as 14.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Tour_of_duty" title="Tour of duty">
        tour of duty
       </a>
       is generally 12 months. The Bolivian government annually spends $130 million on defense.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Bolivian army has around 31,500 men. There are six military regions (
       <i>
        regiones militares
       </i>
       —RMs) in the army. The army is organized into ten divisions.
      </p>
      <p>
       Though it is landlocked Bolivia keeps a navy. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolivian_Naval_Force" title="Bolivian Naval Force">
        Bolivian Naval Force
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Fuerza Naval Boliviana
       </i>
       in Spanish) is a naval force about 5,000 strong in 2008.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_Air_Force" title="Bolivian Air Force">
        Bolivian Air Force
       </a>
       ('Fuerza Aérea Boliviana' or 'FAB') has nine air bases, located at La Paz, Cochabamba,
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_la_Sierra" title="Santa Cruz de la Sierra">
        Santa Cruz
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Su%C3%A1rez" title="Puerto Suárez">
        Puerto Suárez
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tarija,_Bolivia" title="Tarija, Bolivia">
        Tarija
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Villamontes" title="Villamontes">
        Villamontes
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cobija" title="Cobija">
        Cobija
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Riberalta" title="Riberalta">
        Riberalta
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Robor%C3%A9" title="Roboré">
        Roboré
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">
        Administrative divisions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Bolivia" title="Departments of Bolivia">
        Departments of Bolivia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Bolivia" title="Provinces of Bolivia">
        Provinces of Bolivia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Bolivia" title="Municipalities of Bolivia">
        Municipalities of Bolivia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_Bolivia" title="Cantons of Bolivia">
        Cantons of Bolivia
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Native_Community_Lands" title="Native Community Lands">
        Native Community Lands
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Bolivia has nine departments—
       <a href="/wiki/Pando_Department" title="Pando Department">
        Pando
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/La_Paz_Department_(Bolivia)" title="La Paz Department (Bolivia)">
        La Paz
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Beni_Department" title="Beni Department">
        Beni
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Oruro_Department" title="Oruro Department">
        Oruro
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba_Department" title="Cochabamba Department">
        Cochabamba
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Department_(Bolivia)" title="Santa Cruz Department (Bolivia)">
        Santa Cruz
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Potos%C3%AD_Department" title="Potosí Department">
        Potosí
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chuquisaca_Department" title="Chuquisaca Department">
        Chuquisaca
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tarija_Department" title="Tarija Department">
        Tarija
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       According to what is established by the Bolivian Political Constitution, the Law of Autonomies and Decentralization regulates de procedure for the elaboration of Statutes of Autonomy, the transfer and distribution of direct competences between the central government and the autonomous entities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There are four levels of decentralization: Departmental government, constituted by the
       <i>
        Departmental Assembly
       </i>
       , with rights over the legislation of the department. The
       <a href="/wiki/Governor" title="Governor">
        governor
       </a>
       is chosen by
       <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">
        universal suffrage
       </a>
       . Municipal government, constituted by a
       <i>
        Municipal Council
       </i>
       , with rights over the legislation of the municipality. The
       <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">
        mayor
       </a>
       is chosen by universal suffrage. Regional government, formed by several provinces or municipalities of geographical continuity within a department. It is constituted by a
       <i>
        Regional Assembly
       </i>
       . Original indigenous government,
       <a href="/wiki/Self-governance" title="Self-governance">
        self-governance
       </a>
       of original indigenous people on the ancient territories where they live.
      </p>
      <table border="0" cellpadding="3">
       <tr>
        <th>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Bolivia" title="Economy of Bolivia">
        Economy of Bolivia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="864" data-file-width="1106" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg/220px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg/330px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg/440px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Graphical depiction of Bolivia's product exports in 28 color-coded categories
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Bolivia's estimated 2012 gross domestic product (GDP) totaled $27.43 billion at official exchange rate and $56.14 billion at purchasing power parity. Economic growth was estimated to be at about 5.2%, and inflation was estimated at about 6.9%.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Bolivia was rated "Repressed" by
       <a href="/wiki/The_Heritage_Foundation" title="The Heritage Foundation">
        The Heritage Foundation
       </a>
       's 2010
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">
         Index of Economic Freedom
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Despite a series of mostly political setbacks, between 2006 and 2009 the Morales administration has spurred growth higher than at any point in the preceding 30 years. The growth was accompanied by a moderate decrease in inequality.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A surplus budget of 1.7% (GDP) was obtained by 2012, the government runs surpluses since Morales administration reflecting a prudent economic management.
      </p>
      <p>
       A major blow to the Bolivian economy came with a drastic fall in the price of tin during the early 1980s, which impacted one of Bolivia's main sources of income and one of its major mining industries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since 1985, the government of Bolivia has implemented a far-reaching program of macroeconomic stabilization and structural reform aimed at maintaining price stability, creating conditions for sustained growth, and alleviating scarcity. A major reform of the customs service has significantly improved transparency in this area. Parallel legislative reforms have locked into place market-liberal policies, especially in the hydrocarbon and telecommunication sectors, that have encouraged private investment. Foreign investors are accorded national treatment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miners_at_Work_Potosi_(pixinn.net).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="681" data-file-width="1024" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/220px-Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/330px-Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/440px-Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miners_at_Work_Potosi_(pixinn.net).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Young miners at work in
         <a href="/wiki/Potos%C3%AD" title="Potosí">
          Potosí
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macrodistrito_de_Cotahuma,_La_Paz.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Macrodistrito_de_Cotahuma%2C_La_Paz.jpg/220px-Macrodistrito_de_Cotahuma%2C_La_Paz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Macrodistrito_de_Cotahuma%2C_La_Paz.jpg/330px-Macrodistrito_de_Cotahuma%2C_La_Paz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Macrodistrito_de_Cotahuma%2C_La_Paz.jpg/440px-Macrodistrito_de_Cotahuma%2C_La_Paz.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macrodistrito_de_Cotahuma,_La_Paz.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         La Paz is an important administrative and economic center of Bolivia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In April 2000, Hugo Banzer, the former President of Bolivia, signed a contract with Aguas del Tunari, a private consortium, to operate and improve the water supply in Bolivia's third-largest city,
       <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba" title="Cochabamba">
        Cochabamba
       </a>
       . Shortly thereafter, the company tripled the water rates in that city, an action which resulted in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2000_Cochabamba_protests" title="2000 Cochabamba protests">
        protests and rioting
       </a>
       among those who could no longer afford clean water.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Amidst Bolivia's nationwide economic collapse and growing national unrest over the state of the economy, the Bolivian government was forced to withdraw the water contract.
      </p>
      <p>
       Bolivia has the second largest
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">
        natural gas
       </a>
       reserves in South America.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The government has a long-term sales agreement to sell natural gas to Brazil through 2019. The government held a binding referendum in 2005 on the Hydrocarbon Law.
      </p>
      <p>
       The US Geological Service estimates that Bolivia has 5.4 million
       <a href="/wiki/Cubic_ton" title="Cubic ton">
        cubic tonnes
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Lithium" title="Lithium">
        lithium
       </a>
       , which represent 50%–70% of world reserves. However, to mine for it would involve disturbing the country's salt flats (called
       <a href="/wiki/Salar_de_Uyuni" title="Salar de Uyuni">
        Salar de Uyuni
       </a>
       ), an important natural feature which boosts tourism in the region. The government does not want to destroy this unique natural landscape to meet the rising world demand for lithium.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On the other hand, sustainable extraction of lithium is attempted by the government. This project is carried out by the public company "Recursos Evaporíticos" subsidiary of COMIBOL.
      </p>
      <p>
       Once Bolivia's government depended heavily on foreign assistance to finance development projects and to pay the public staff. At the end of 2002, the government owed $4.5 billion to its foreign
       <a href="/wiki/Creditor" title="Creditor">
        creditors
       </a>
       , with $1.6 billion of this amount owed to other governments and most of the balance owed to multilateral development banks. Most payments to other governments have been rescheduled on several occasions since 1987 through the
       <a href="/wiki/Paris_Club" title="Paris Club">
        Paris Club
       </a>
       mechanism. External creditors have been willing to do this because the Bolivian government has generally achieved the monetary and fiscal targets set by IMF programs since 1987, though economic crises have undercut Bolivia's normally good record. However, by 2013 the foreign assistance is just a fraction of the government budget thanks to tax collection mainly from the profitable exports to Brazil and Argentina of natural gas.
      </p>
      <p>
       The income from tourism has become increasingly important.
       <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Bolivia" title="Tourism in Bolivia">
        Bolivia's tourist industry
       </a>
       has grown gradually since about 1990.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign-exchange_reserves">
        Foreign-exchange reserves
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Foreign-exchange reserves">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The amount in reserve currencies and
       <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">
        gold
       </a>
       held by Bolivia's Central Bank advanced from 1.085 billion US dollars in 2000, under
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hugo_Banzer_Suarez" title="Hugo Banzer Suarez">
        Hugo Banzer Suarez
       </a>
       's government, to 15.282 billion US dollars in 2014 under
       <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">
        Evo Morales
       </a>
       ' government.
      </p>
      <table style="margin: 1em auto; padding: 0.5e text-align:left; clear:all; font-size:90%">
       <tr>
        <td colspan="6" style="background:#black; color:white; text-align: center; background-color: #9acd32;">

          </span>
         </b>
         <b>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
           <a href="#cite_note-69">
            [69]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </b>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <div class="timeline-wrapper">

         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td align="center" colspan="1" style="background:#f5f5f5;">
